Japanese Troops in East and West River Areas of Guangdong Support the Japanese Troops Invading Southern Guangdong, Again Stirring on the Guangzhou-Kowloon Railway Line, Threatening to Attack Zhongshan Again on a Set Date

Hong Kong Correspondence - Japanese troops entrenched in various places in the East, West, and North River areas and Jiangmen and Xinhui, in order to respond to the invasion of Southern Guangdong and contain Chinese military forces, have been stirring up trouble in recent days. The following is a record of their actions:

East River Area

Japanese troops stationed on the south bank of the East River in Dongguan and Baoan have been dispatched from Shilong and Shenzhen since the 18th, attempting to attack the central section of the Guangzhou-Kowloon Railway from the north and south, and then open up the entire line. Their ambitions are great, and their momentum is fierce. On the morning of the 18th, when the Japanese troops in Shenzhen attacked northward, more than 500 Japanese troops, including infantry and cavalry, with several cannons, crossed the Jinshui River and attacked the positions of the Chinese army in Hengli and Tutang, along with the Tea Mountain, Nanshe, and puppet troops. The regular Chinese army Chen regiment, the security force Zhang regiment, and the guerrilla Liu unit, which were guarding the area, separately intercepted them at key points. The Japanese army first bombarded the Chinese positions with artillery fire and advanced with cavalry to cover the infantry. The Chinese army calmly responded under the fierce artillery fire and aerial bombardment of the Japanese army. The Japanese army charged several times but could not cross the Chinese defense line. In the evening, the Japanese army, seeing that the Chinese positions were strong and suffering heavy casualties, was forced to retreat and collapsed towards Chashan Jing Mountain. The Chinese army took advantage of the victory to pursue them. On the morning of the 19th, the Japanese army, knowing that it was difficult to succeed, mostly fled back to Shilong. The Chinese army is still searching for remnants and deploying new positions in Chashan and Nanshe to prevent the Japanese army from launching another attack. In this battle, the Japanese army suffered more than 200 casualties and left more than 50 corpses. As for the Japanese troops who attacked northward along the Sha-Shen and Guangzhou-Kowloon roads from Shenzhen, they were intercepted by the Chinese army Yu Brigade, Yun Chunlin, Chen Division, and Ni Dingyuan on the 18th and 19th, and fierce battles were fought at Tiantangwei Ferry and other places. The Japanese army suffered 400 to 500 casualties. On the afternoon of the 19th, the Chinese army in Qingxi, Tangxia, Longgang, and other places joined the battle and launched a counterattack against the Japanese army. The Japanese army could not resist. By evening, the Japanese troops near Hengkang had returned to Shawan, and the Japanese troops on the Guangzhou-Kowloon front had also crossed the river from Tiantangwei and moved back to Pinghu and Buji. The Chinese army Yu Brigade and Yun Regiment took advantage of the situation and advanced, with the vanguard once crossing Pinghu and engaging in a night battle with more than 100 Japanese troops. Later, due to strategic considerations, they retreated to their original positions. On the 20th, just after dawn, four Japanese planes flew from the sea off Dachan, covering the Japanese troops in Pinghu and Shawan and continuing to retreat to Shenzhen. The Japanese planes then flew over the Guangzhou-Kowloon, Sha-Shen, Hui-Zhang, and Ping-Tan lines to reconnoiter and dropped bombs on Tangxia, Qingxi, Lin Village, Hengli, and other places. Chinese losses are unknown. After the Japanese army captured Nantou and Shenzhen, they repeatedly attempted to open up the Guangzhou-Kowloon Railway and occupy Shark Bay, Kwai Tung, and Salt Field to cut off the Chinese army's external communication and liaison in the East River area. The Chinese military authorities, aware of the Japanese army's conspiracy, have been continuously dispatching large forces to the counties of Dong, Bao, and Hui to increase defenses. It is now learned that Xiang Hanping, Deputy Commander-in-Chief and Director of the Guerrilla Command Post of the 9th Army Group, who is responsible for military affairs in the East River area, believes that the Japanese army launched two-way attacks from Shilong and Shenzhen this time to attack the Chinese army in order to open up the Guangzhou-Kowloon Railway and invade Huiyang. Fortunately, the officers and soldiers of various units bravely resisted and inflicted heavy blows on the Japanese army. However, the Japanese army's ambitions have not diminished, and it is difficult to guarantee that they will not seize the opportunity to launch another attack. In order to strengthen the military strength in Dong and Bao and tighten control over the Japanese army, a cable has been sent to the Fourth War Zone authorities to dispatch a large army to increase defenses in various places and redeploy the offensive and defensive positions on the Guangzhou-Kowloon, Sha-Shen, Hui-Zhang, and Ping-Long lines in order to be able to attack and encircle and annihilate the Japanese army in order to consolidate the defense on the south bank of the East River.

West River Area

Japanese troops in the lower reaches of the West River have been frequently mobilized in the past week. Japanese military vehicles travel daily on the Guangzhou-Sanshui line from Guangzhou to Foshan, and the carriage windows are tightly closed when traveling, which seems very secretive. In addition, Japanese troops in Sanshui, Southwest, Hekou, Makou, and other places have been transferred to Foshan, Jiujiang, and other places in recent days. The number of Japanese troops in Jiujiang, Heqing, Honglou, Longchi Jitang, Datang, and other places has slightly increased. More than 100 Japanese engineers have been actively strengthening fortifications in the Da Gang and Chongliang Gang areas near Jiujiang. Two Japanese shallow-water warships are moored on the Jiujiang Shakou River. More than 50 Japanese motorboats and rubber boats travel daily on the waterway from Shakou to Jiangmen, transporting grain and military supplies. Obviously, there are plans for invasion on the West River.

Jiang-Hui Area

After the Japanese army began invading Qinlian, they instigated traitors to spread rumors everywhere, saying that they would attack Zhongshan again before the 20th of this month and seize Sanbu, the throat of Siyi, on a certain date. The leaflets dropped by Japanese planes in Zhongshan County also made the same propaganda, hoping to shake people's hearts. The Chinese military authorities, upon receiving the report, ordered a certain unit of the Western Front assault force to advance towards Mulang along the Xin-He Line. In order to prevent the Chinese army from advancing, the Japanese artillery at Foziao continuously fired remotely at the Chinese army positions in Duruan and Ximao Mountain. On the morning of the 17th, the Japanese army took advantage of the heavy fog to launch a counterattack against the Chinese army at Gelao Huai and invaded Zhongshan at the same time. As a result, they were repelled. On the night of the 19th, the moonlight was dim, and the Japanese army, fearing a night attack by the Chinese army, had a Japanese plane fly over the border of Zhongshan and directly to the Xin-He Line, circling for several hours in the Jinggen, Duruan, Pingdi Ling, Ximao Mountain, and Niushan areas, hoping to intimidate the Chinese guerrillas. After the Japanese army's invasion of Xikeng on the Xinkai Line failed, there have been no major movements in the past two days.

Guangdong Provincial Chinese Army Presses Attack on Chaoan; Commander of Japanese Troops in Chenghai Killed; Japanese Aircraft Harass Various Places Repeatedly

Shantou Correspondence - Japanese troops in Chaoan, under the control of Chinese artillery at Zhugaoshan, have not invaded Fengxi for many days. It was not until the 5th that they launched an attack on the Chinese positions by land and sea, and aircraft were dispatched from Shantou to fight. Two planes dropped bombs on Yixi, Hulushi, Wenshi City, Zhangwang and other villages, and strafed the Yixi-Fenghuang Highway, destroying more than 30 civilian houses, killing and wounding more than ten people, and bombing seven oxen to death. In the afternoon, Chinese reinforcements from Fengshun arrived and crossed the Shipailou Zhuhang on the same night, surrounding and attacking the Japanese troops in Qiulang Mountain and Hulushi. The Japanese troops were quite chaotic. More than 300 people entered Yixi and were all wiped out. The 5th Battalion of the Raoping Chinese Army and part of the Security Force responded across the river, pressing the attack on Hanshan Weicun and surrounding more than 100 Japanese troops in the village. After about an hour of fierce fighting, 60 to 70 people were beheaded and captured. The Japanese troops stationed in Hanshan rushed to the scene, and the Chinese army immediately withdrew. After the 6th, the Chinese army returned to its original positions, erected troops and cannons at Qiulang Mountain and Zhugaoshan, and exchanged artillery fire with the Japanese troops in Hanshan. On the same day, three Japanese planes flew to Xingning County and dropped four bombs, destroying more than ten shops, killing five people, and wounding several people. Another two planes dropped six bombs in Tangkeng Jiuzhaizhai, Fengshun. Also, at 8:00 AM on the same day, another five Japanese planes flew to Raoping, Zhaolin, and Huanggang and dropped more than ten bombs, killing and wounding more than ten civilians.

On the 5th, the puppet pacification troops stationed in Chenghai City gathered at the county middle school playground for inspection. When the Japanese commander Nakamura was standing on the stage giving a speech, gunshots suddenly rang out in front of the stage. It turned out that the Chinese plainclothes team had rushed in and killed Nakamura on the spot. Translator Lin Taisanmen was seriously injured. After this blow, the Japanese army detained all the puppet troops who were inspected in the Chenghuang Temple, dispatched more than 300 Japanese troops to closely monitor the 5th Regiment of the puppet army, and transferred 200 people to Anbu to disperse the strength of the puppet army. On the 7th, the Chinese army's counterattack on Chaoan was very urgent, and the Japanese army urgently mobilized 200 cavalry and 500 to 600 infantry to deploy outside Shantou. In front of the Shantou Customs, there were only two or three Japanese warships moored. On the morning of the 8th, two transport ships entered the port, transporting 700 to 800 Japanese troops. In the afternoon, the number of Japanese warships continued to increase, unloading military supplies and grain to land. On the morning of the 9th, there were 13 Japanese warships in Shantou Port, moored in Nan'ao, Dahao, and Tuojiang Estuary. At 2:00 PM in the afternoon, five Japanese fast armored boats transported more than 200 Japanese soldiers into the Hanjiang tributary to reinforce the defense of Chenghai Chaoan. The Horino Command Headquarters stationed in Anbu has been moved to Zhongshan Park. Judging from the hurried dispatch and mobilization of the Japanese army, it is evident that the fighting in the Chaoan area is intensifying.

According to those who fled to Shantou, the Japanese army suffered a disastrous defeat in Yixi on the 5th, with more than 400 to 500 killed and wounded, resulting in huge losses. The Japanese army was unwilling to accept this, and from the 8th, the artillery at Hulushan bombarded the villages of Yixi, Qiulang Mountain, Zhuhang, and Wenshi City from afar. Fifteen Japanese planes also flew to the highways of Meixian, Pingyuan, Xunwu, and Xingning and dropped bombs. Twenty bombs were dropped on Pingyuan, Datuo, and Bachih. Also, when Japanese planes arrived in Meixian, the Chinese air defense forces engaged in an air-to-ground battle on a certain mountaintop. After 30 minutes, two Japanese planes were hit and emitted white smoke and fled in embarrassment. On the 9th, artillery battles broke out again in the suburbs of Chaoan. Fifteen Japanese planes flew out again to harass the rear of the Chinese army, dropping more than 20 huge bombs in Meixian and Xingning, circling the Mei-Song Road and Mei-Xing Road for five hours, and firing wildly at passing boats and vehicles. In the second time, five planes arrived in Meicheng, and two or thirty large houses of various surnames in the market were destroyed. Seventy to eighty civilians were killed or injured. Chenghuang and Tang, Pankeng Tian were also bombed. On the evening of the 9th, the Fengshun Chinese artillery arrived at Yixi Qiulang Mountain and fired remotely at Chaoan City, destroying many Japanese positions, with eight out of ten hits. On the same night, the Chinese army set out from Zhuhang, bypassed Fengxi, and engaged in battle with more than 200 Japanese troops on the Anjie Highway outside the South Gate at 2:00 AM on the 10th, advancing into West Lake and engaging in a bloody battle. The Chinese artillery at Zhugaoshan fully exerted its power to assist in attacking the North Gate. A cavalry unit of 120 men, wielding spears and broadswords, charged into the Japanese barracks at Chuncheng Tower in the South Gate. Fifty Japanese troops stationed there were all stabbed to death by spears. The bloody battle continued until dawn, and the Chinese army retreated. Both sides only had artillery battles. A large-scale battle is about to break out within days outside the city of Chaozhou.

Shanghai Four Banks Handle Debt Donation; Citizens Should Unite in Contributions; Not a Small Benefit to the Future of the War of Resistance; Four Banks Set Up Specialized Departments to Accept Debt Donations

The New Life Movement Promotion Association recently launched a debt donation campaign. The Central Bank of China, the Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, and the Farmers Bank of China have volunteered to handle the reception of this debt donation work to promote it. The Bank of China handles this matter on behalf of Hong Kong and overseas locations. The Shanghai branches of the four banks have set up specialized departments to handle this. The details are as follows:

The New Life Movement Advocates for a Debt Donation Campaign

The New Life Movement Promotion Association, in view of the fact that after the outbreak of the Japanese invasion of China, the government authorities, in order to concentrate financial resources, prepare for a long-term war of resistance, and lay the foundation for final victory, have successively issued National Salvation Bonds, National Defense Bonds, and Gold Bonds during this period of war. The people of the whole country unanimously support the leader, support the national policy of resisting aggression and building the nation, and are enthusiastically involved in purchasing these bonds. People from friendly countries overseas who sympathize with China's war of resistance also purchased Chinese bonds. In order to maintain creditworthiness, the government issued bond interest on schedule in accordance with the regulations. Now, in order to reduce the government's financial burden and gather more funds to continue the war of resistance, the association has launched a debt donation campaign, asking the people and people from friendly countries who hold these bonds to voluntarily donate them to the National Government. It is of no small benefit to the war of resistance, and its significance is particularly significant.

The Four Banks Volunteer to Handle It

The head offices of the Central Bank of China, Bank of China, Bank of Communications, and the Farmers Bank of China, believing that the debt donation campaign has been launched by the New Life Movement, have already volunteered to handle the reception of this debt donation work in order to assist and promote this matter. On the one hand, they were ordered by the central government to order their branches and offices in various provinces and cities across the country to start handling this work at the same time. As for Hong Kong and overseas countries, the branches of the Bank of China in various countries are fully authorized to handle this matter.

Shanghai Four Branches Obey Orders and Handle Debt Donations

According to the Shanghai branches of the four banks, the head office has already ordered the commencement of this debt donation work. In addition to the Bank of China ordering the National Treasury to handle it, the other three branches of the Central, Bank of Communications, and the Farmers Bank of China have set up specialized departments to handle this matter. Regarding the debt donation method, if Chinese and foreigners hold these bonds and present them to the four banks, the handling bank may issue a temporary receipt. On the one hand, they will collect the bond certificates and numbers and submit them to the head office authorities. Then, they will submit them to the National Treasury for safekeeping. On the one hand, they will cancel the bond rights held by the debt donors one by one, and the lottery numbers of the bonds that are due in the future will no longer be included. The procedures are very simple. I hope that all bondholders will actively promote this righteous act of debt donation.

Japanese Plan to Widen the Yunzaobing to Convert it into a Commercial Port

Yunzaobing is the only inland river in Wusong, with a width of more than twenty feet, stretching westward for dozens of miles, directly to Changshu and Kunshan. Since the fall of the Song District, it has been occupied by the Japanese army and used as a military food zone. It is now learned that the Japanese plan to convert Yunzaobing into a commercial port, widening the river surface by about sixty feet, and building wharves and warehouses next to it, in an attempt to restore its former prosperity and make it a base for dumping Japanese goods.

Japanese Deny Searching British Residence; British Consulate Confirms Protest

At 3:00 AM on the 23rd of this month, six Japanese Naval Landing Force sailors suddenly broke down the door of the residence of British citizen Mr. Santos, located at No. 24, Lane 506, North Sichuan Road, and searched the premises. However, even though Mr. Santos showed them his British passport, they ignored it. Last night, a Japanese naval spokesman denied at a press briefing that the Marine Corps had searched the aforementioned residence. It was claimed that the searched residence was located in the Huajie Liuxiang area. Residences in and around that area are regularly searched by Marine Corps members. Marine Corps searchers try their best to avoid making foreign residents uncomfortable, so they immediately withdraw when they encounter foreign residences and do not enter, etc. According to reports, the incident on the 23rd was that six members of the Japanese Marine Corps entered Mr. Santos' residence. Mr. Santos initially refused, but then showed his passport, but the Japanese soldiers did not listen and pushed Mr. Santos aside, thoroughly searching the house. Afterwards, the British Consulate protested.

Shanghai Manufactured Products Prohibited from Being Sold in the Interior; National Goods Industry Attaches Importance; Does it Include the Concession Area? National Goods Organizations Cable Authorities for Inquiry

The Shanghai National Goods Industry has attached importance to the report that Chongqing has cabled that the Ministry of Economic Affairs has ordered that, from now on, manufactured products from the occupied areas, including those manufactured in Shanghai, are not allowed to be imported into the areas controlled by the Chinese government. The various national goods organizations will cable the authorities to inquire whether the so-called "including those manufactured in Shanghai" also includes the concession area. After the war, the sales of Shanghai national goods manufacturers in the interior were very difficult due to traffic obstructions. Only the South Seas still had considerable monthly sales. If sales in the interior are now prohibited, then they will have no place to stand. However, the authorities' adoption of this policy is actually a countermeasure against Japanese goods being falsely labeled as national goods and mixed in the interior, destroying the war economy, and they have no choice but to take this measure.

Overseas Chinese from Fujian Return to Southeast Asia to Continue Business

A large number of overseas Chinese residing in Southeast Asia are engaged in business. Since the start of the Sino-Japanese War, these compatriots have been particularly concerned about the situation of the war in their homeland. When the Japanese army invaded Guangdong and Fujian provinces last year, the Guangdong and Fujian overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia returned to their motherland to engage in various wartime tasks to defend their hometowns. At that time, no less than several thousand overseas Chinese from Fujian returned to the country from Southeast Asia. Later, with the fall of Xiamen, traffic between the province and Southeast Asia was suddenly blocked. The overseas Chinese could neither return to Southeast Asia nor develop in the interior, so they moved to Quanzhou, Xinghua and other places. It is now known that these overseas Chinese still have businesses in Southeast Asia, and since returning to the country, it has been almost a year. Now that the navigation between Xinghua, Quanzhou and Shanghai has also been restored, they are rushing to Shanghai by boat, preparing to transfer to Southeast Asia to continue their business. More than 700 people have arrived in Shanghai in recent days. They are being received separately by the Shanxi, Jinjiang, and Hui'an fellow-townsmen associations in Shanghai and are lodging in hotels. The first batch of more than 300 people are scheduled to take the Java Mail Steamship Company's "Tjisadane" on the 30th of this month, departing from Shanghai directly to Southeast Asia to continue their business.

Gold Public Bonds, National Defense Public Bonds: Overseas Payment Methods; Not Entrusting Other Overseas Branches of the Bank of China for the Time Being; The Receiving Bank Will Take Payment From the Bank of Communications

The Ministry of Finance issued a circular to overseas Chinese organizations stating that the first redemption of principal and interest for the 1938 Gold Public Bonds and National Defense Public Bonds will be on October 31st of this year. All matters concerning the redemption of principal and interest, regarding the Gold Public Bonds, the overseas portion will be managed and paid by the four banks, the Hong Kong branch, or other overseas branches of the Bank of China. Regarding the National Defense Public Bonds, the overseas portion will be entrusted by the Central Bank to the Hong Kong branches of the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications, or other overseas branches of the two banks, for management and payment. The Ministry has already issued a letter on October 23rd to check and act accordingly. Now, due to the fact that the redemption of principal and interest for the overseas portion will not be entrusted to other overseas branches of the Bank of China for the time being, overseas Chinese holding the above-mentioned winning bond tickets and matured interest coupons can withdraw the principal and interest according to the following methods: (1) Regarding the Gold Public Bonds, the winning bond tickets and matured interest coupons should be entrusted to the previously designated receiving banks (i.e., the Bank of China, Guangdong Bank, Overseas Chinese Bank, China Revitalization Bank, and East Asia Bank) to collect the principal and interest from the Hong Kong branches of the Central Bank, the Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, and the Farmers Bank. (2) Regarding the National Defense Public Bonds, the winning bond tickets and matured interest coupons should be entrusted to the previously designated receiving banks (i.e., the Bank of China, Guangdong Bank, Overseas Chinese Bank, China Revitalization Bank, and East Asia Bank) to collect the principal and interest from the Hong Kong branch of the Bank of China or the Bank of Communications. In addition to separate circulars, it is hereby notified so that you may check and handle accordingly.

Lack of Subsidiary Currency Notes: Remedial Measures Have Been Devised; The Bank of China, Bank of Communications, Farmers Bank Cooperating; Implementation After Approval From the Central Headquarters; Five-Jiao and Two-Jiao-Five-Fen Notes to Be Exchanged As Much As Possible

After the panic over the lack of subsidiary currency notes and fractional currency notes in the Shanghai market, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce has sent a letter to the Shanghai branch of the Central Bank to find ways to regulate the situation. A reporter from the "New Voice News Agency" learned from banking circles yesterday that the subsidiary currency notes circulating in the Shanghai market are issued by the Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, the Farmers Bank, and the Jiangsu Farmers Bank, Zhejiang Local Bank, and others, in large quantities, which are sufficient for market circulation. The recent panic over the lack is obviously due to someone hoarding for profit.

#### Total Amount of Jiao Currency Issued Last Month

In the middle of last month, the Shanghai branch of the Central Bank issued a total of 3.5 million yuan of new one-jiao and two-jiao subsidiary currency notes. Now, only a few weeks later, there is such a phenomenon of scarcity, which is completely unexpected. As for the fractional currency notes, the first batch issued was 500,000 yuan, which should have been sufficient for the market's needs for small change, but now it is also scarce, which is also unexpected.

#### Four Banks Together Devise Remedial Measures

Currently, the Shanghai branch of the Central Bank has cooperated with the Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, the Farmers Bank, and other banks to devise remedial measures. In addition to the Farmers Bank of China first exchanging and circulating the five-jiao subsidiary currency notes in stock as much as possible, the remedial measures will be implemented after approval from the head office, and will be publicly announced.

#### Arrival of Fractional Currency Notes: Another Announcement in Shanghai

As for the Farmers Bank of China's daily exchange and issuance of five-jiao subsidiary currency notes, the amount is about 100,000 yuan. Because the bank's address is on Avenue Joffre, and the bank's premises are not spacious, and the number of exchangers is crowded, the exchange procedure has been moved to the Central Bank at 439 Avenue Albert beginning today (the 28th). The time is from 9:00 AM to 12:00 noon every day. The second batch of fractional currency notes has been contracted to be printed by the American-owned Wing On Company. After printing is completed, the Shanghai branch of the Central Bank will publicly announce the issuance, so the panic over the lack of subsidiary currency notes and fractional currency notes will soon be eliminated.

A Large Batch of Wuhu Xian Rice Will Arrive in Shanghai for Sale; Transactions in the Rice Market Tend to Stabilize; Market Prices Are Not Worthy of Attention

The rising trend of rice prices in recent days, after serious expressions from various bodies and powerful people, has been slightly curbed, but has not fallen, so the panic over food rice has still not been relieved. The number of arrivals by land and water per day is six to seven thousand bags, which is comparable to the amount of food rice needed by the city's residents every day. The Wuhu xian rice, which was previously controlled by Japanese merchants, can now be freely transported to Shanghai, and a large batch of Wuhu xian rice will arrive in Shanghai for sale in the near future. Rice shops have been sluggish in their intake due to the high price of rice, while rice dealers have also been actively transporting rice due to the profitable increase in rice prices in the Shanghai market. It is expected that a large batch of domestic rice will come to Shanghai from the interior soon. The Brokers Association has been advised to stop its members from short selling and buying empty in the market after the Rice Market Management Committee resolved to prohibit brokers from speculating and artificially raising prices. It is also advising members not to engage in such bad practices in the market. Therefore, in the context of abundant arrivals, sluggish intake, and stable market transactions in the Shanghai rice market, prices will inevitably fall in the near future. The reason why rice prices have not yet fallen is that rice merchants are attempting to hoard goods purchased at high prices and are unwilling to sell at lower prices.

Customs Releases National Trade Figures for the Past Three Years; After Efforts to Adjust, The State of Pre-War Recovery

The customs released trade import and export figures for the past three years: (1) From January to October of the 26th year of the Republic [1937], imports were valued at 85,609,463 yuan, and exports were valued at 73,275,6914 yuan. (2) From January to October of the 27th year of the Republic [1938], imports were valued at 73,972,2005 yuan, and exports were valued at 63,600,09325 yuan. (3) From January to October of the 28th year of the Republic [1939], imports were valued at 116,140,06799 yuan, and exports were valued at 77,161,6551 yuan. This is sufficient evidence that China's foreign trade, after government adjustments, has recovered to its pre-war state, and trade has improved since September of this year, with the excess of imports over exports gradually decreasing. The elimination of the excess of imports over exports at the Shanghai Customs has been successfully achieved.

Shanghai's Weather is Extremely Cold; A Warm-Up is Expected Today; The High Pressure Has Passed Shanghai and a Warm-Up is Possible; Over Forty More People Froze to Death Yesterday

Since the Siberian high-pressure system pushed towards central China, the weather in Shanghai and the lower reaches of the Yangtze River has become extremely cold with strong northerly winds. Around 6:00 AM yesterday, the temperature in Shanghai, according to the Xujiahui Observatory, plummeted to -4.1 degrees Celsius (the day before it was only -2.2 degrees Celsius), which is around 28 degrees Fahrenheit, making it the first extremely cold day of the winter. As a result, the ditches were frozen solid, as were water containers. Although water did not freeze instantly, breath turned into clouds. According to the observatory's forecast, the high-pressure system that struck Shanghai is now moving southeast and is expected to leave Shanghai, so the weather is expected to warm up slightly today. Due to the extreme cold, the number of boats on the Suzhou Creek suddenly decreased today, likely due to the river freezing. Many refugees and beggars froze to death, and pedestrians on the street were shivering from the cold air.

People Freeze to Death on the Streets: Over Forty More

Since the sudden cold snap the day before yesterday, over fifty homeless beggars and refugees have frozen to death on the streets within the two foreign concessions. The situation is extremely dire. Yesterday, due to the persistent cold wave, over forty more refugees and beggars, lacking warm clothing, froze to death. According to the Pushan Villa report, twenty-eight people died within the Public Concession. As of the time of this dispatch, two burial vehicles from Pushan Villa were still out collecting bodies, so the total number is likely higher. The Tongren Fuyuan Hall reported that seventeen or eighteen refugee beggars had frozen to death within the French Concession, so the total number is approximately forty-five or forty-six.

Investigation of Locations Where Refugees and Beggars Froze to Death

(French Concession) One person near Zhengjia Bridge, one person on Mofang Street, one person on Maidian Road, one person on East Zilaihuo Street, one person on West Zilaihuo Street, and over ten people in other locations, totaling approximately seventeen or eighteen people. A Korean Woman Was Strangled to Death; Her Hands and Feet Were Bound; Her Mouth Was Stuffed with Cotton

A Korean man named Bu, around forty years old, worked as a ticket inspector number 14 for the Public Concession tram company. His wife, Luo, around thirty years old, also Korean, lived with him at 432 Father Rhodes Road in the French Concession. Bu has a daughter who attends a nearby primary school. Yesterday afternoon around 4:00 PM, the daughter returned home from school and knocked on the door for a long time, but there was no response. The child was terrified and cried. Neighbors saw this and helped knock on the door, but there was still no response. They had no choice but to find a way to pry open the door. They found Luo lying dead in the house, her hands and feet tightly bound with rope, a thick rope wrapped around her neck, and her mouth stuffed with cotton. They realized she had been murdered. Someone reported it to the police station, and investigators from the Japanese consulate went to investigate. It was reported that only Luo was in the house at the time, and Bu had gone to work. The police are still investigating the circumstances of the murder.

A Robber Used a Fake Gun; Both the Person and the Goods Were Captured

At around 6:15 PM yesterday, a residence with the surname Mou at number 7 Baoxing Village on Shanhai Pass Road was tricked into opening the door by a robber who entered and committed robbery. The people in the house, seeing that the robber had a weapon, did not dare to move or make a sound. As a result, they were robbed of jewelry, cash, and other items totaling over five hundred yuan. After the robber left the house, the residents suddenly realized that the handgun he was carrying was a fake. They quickly chased after him, calling for help. Patrol officers heard this and immediately arrived to intercept the robber. Seeing that the robber was trying to escape, they fired a total of eight shots, hitting and capturing the robber. They seized the fake gun and recovered the stolen goods from the robber, and then escorted him to the police station for detention.

At around 2:00 AM yesterday, seven robbers, three of whom were armed with handguns, robbed house number 2, Lane 163, of the extraterritorial section of Robert Road in West Shanghai. Woman Sentenced to Five Years for Selling Opium

Zhao Chenshi, the 34-year-old wife of Zhao Xinmei, a gambler from Pudong who lives at 140 Dongmu Laihuo Street in the French Concession, hid 78 packages of opium, each package weighing one tael, and three large packages of morphine, worth over one thousand yuan, inside a hidden compartment in a handbag on the morning of the 6th of this month. She planned to take them to the countryside in Pudong to sell for profit. She hired a rickshaw to go to the Bund to board a ferry to Pupu. While passing the intersection of Fazada Road and Zilai Street, she was discovered by patrol officers who checked pedestrians. The opium and drug evidence were seized and she was taken to the police station. According to her confession, the opium was purchased on her behalf by Zhu Yiqing (61 years old) from Ju Township in room 414 of the East Asia Hotel. Zhu was subsequently arrested and sent to the First Special Court for prosecution. Chenshi confessed to drug trafficking. Zhu claimed that the opium was bought by Chenshi's husband, and that her husband was in his room but only asked him to answer the phone and did not buy opium on his behalf. He hired lawyer Wang Shizong to defend him. The case has already been concluded. Yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM, Judge Zhang Minsheng delivered the verdict: Zhao Chenshi was sentenced to five years of imprisonment and deprived of public rights for five years; Zhu Yiqing was found not guilty. During the appeal period, Zhao Chenshi was detained in the detention center, and Zhu Yiqing was released on a shop bail of three thousand yuan.

(Special Dispatch from Northern Jiangsu) The Jiangsu Education Department recently compiled a detailed statistical report on the income and expenditure of provincial and county education funds in Jiangsu Province for the twenty-seventh year. The following is a summary:

(A) Provincial Education Funds

Revenue: Regular Funds: "Provincial Education Special Funds Revenue," budgeted at 69,496.00 yuan, actual revenue 174,908.14 yuan; "Tuition and Miscellaneous Fees Revenue from Provincial Temporary Secondary Schools," budgeted at 9,120.00 yuan, actual revenue 6,406.00 yuan. Total budgeted revenue: 78,616.00 yuan, actual revenue: 181,314.14 yuan. Temporary Funds: "Use of Surplus from Jiangsu Bank Provincial Education Special Funds," budgeted at 19,800.00 yuan. Total budgeted revenue: 98,416.00 yuan, actual revenue: 181,314.14 yuan. The increase totaled 82,898.14 yuan. (Note: (1) The original budget was calculated by academic year, but in accounting terms, it was the budget for the six months from August to December of the twenty-seventh year and January of the twenty-eighth year. (2) Actual revenue is from July 28 to the end of December of the twenty-seventh year. (3) Of the 174,908.14 yuan in actual revenue from the Provincial Education Special Funds, 136,677.14 yuan was actually received by the management office, and 11,231.00 yuan was directly disbursed by the county governments.)

Expenditures: Regular Funds: "Secondary Education Expenses," budgeted at 62,556.00 yuan, actual expenditure 38,468.00 yuan; "Elementary Education Expenses," budgeted at 15,360.00 yuan, actual expenditure 12,288.00 yuan; "Custody Fees for Custodial Institutions," budgeted at 5,700.00 yuan, actual expenditure 4,175.00 yuan. Total budgeted expenditure: 83,616.00 yuan, actual expenditure: 54,931.00 yuan. Temporary Funds: "Temporary Expenses for Repairs of Various Institutions," both budgeted and actually spent at 4,800.00 yuan; "Reserve Funds," budgeted at 10,000.00 yuan, actual expenditure 2,926.62 yuan. Total budgeted expenditure: 14,800.00 yuan, actual expenditure: 7,729.62 yuan. Total budgeted expenditure: 98,416.00 yuan, actual expenditure: 62,660.62 yuan.

(Note) (1) Same as above. (2) Actual expenditure refers to the amount withdrawn from the treasury and transferred, from August to the end of December of the twenty-seventh year. (3) The subsidy of 1,650 yuan for a certain middle school for five months within the secondary education expenses was advanced by Director Zhao of the Finance Department and is not included in the above actual expenditure. (4) The additional class fees for various schools are included in the regular expenses and are not included in the above reserve funds.) The balance between the above income and expenditure is 118,653.52 yuan.

Shanghai: A Glimpse of Talent Supply and Demand Two Years After the War (9)

— Pan Wen'an, Zheng Wenhan, Shen Guanglie

Conclusion

Based on the above comparative analysis, the following general conclusions can be drawn regarding the actual situation of talent supply and demand in Shanghai:

(1) The ratio of job opportunities to the number of job seekers has increased compared to both before the war and the first year after the war, accounting for about 10 to 8. However, the proportion of people who successfully find employment is less than one-third, which is similar to the past. The severity of unemployment has not yet decreased.

(2) Comparing the types of opportunities with the abilities of the talent, the former has the most opportunities in commerce, transportation technology, and crafts, while the latter has the most talent in commerce, education, and literary affairs. There are many mismatches between supply and demand, so the chances of success are also reduced.

(3) The number of male job seekers is about four and a half times more than female job seekers, which is a decrease from the previous year but still higher than before the war. The ratio of male to female job seekers is slightly higher than the ratio of male to female opportunities, but these slight differences do not indicate that it is easier for women to find jobs than men.

(4) The expected compensation of job seekers is even lower than in the previous year, but the treatment that employers are willing to offer is still lower than what job seekers expect. With the current soaring prices in Shanghai and the cost of living being several times higher, few people can maintain their lives with such low compensation, which affects job stability and work efficiency.

(5) The opportunities for talent demand in the inland areas are increasing daily, more than tenfold compared to the previous year, with the most demand for technical talent. The compensation is also higher than in Shanghai. Job seekers with specialized skills, if willing to endure hardship and take risks, can more easily find suitable work in the inland areas.

The supply and demand of talent is a major national issue. More than two years have passed since the end of the war, but there are still no concrete measures for the control and distribution of national talent, which is regrettable. The conclusion of this article that the supply and demand of talent is mismatched shows that the seriousness of this problem still exists and is likely not limited to Shanghai alone. How to investigate and statistically analyze national talent, how to properly adjust it, and how to allocate and utilize it so that everyone can use their talents and serve the country is a decisive factor for the future of the war. It is hoped that the authorities will carefully plan and seek a solution to the problem from the overall perspective. In addition, if employers can determine compensation based on work efficiency and the cost of living, and job seekers can focus on acquiring specialized skills and cultivating service ethics, the problem of talent supply and demand will be easily solved. (End)

The affairs, academic, and training departments of Xinbei Middle School on Jiaozhou Road in this city issued a message stating that after the original principal Xu Youpei left Shanghai for some reason in August of this year, Wang Xinming, principal of Binhai Middle School, was appointed as the new principal. International Table Tennis League: Divided into Six Groups for Competition; Sixty Teams Have Already Registered

The Shanghai International Table Tennis Federation held a committee meeting yesterday at the Western Overseas Chinese Youth Association and decided to divide the upcoming league into six groups for competition, including five men's groups and one women's group. Each winning team will receive a medal and keep the silver cup for one year. If the silver cup cannot be raised, it will be canceled. The top two teams in each group will be promoted to a higher group, and the bottom two teams will be relegated to a lower group. Sixty Chinese and Western teams have already registered for the competition, and it is expected to be a resounding success. The committee will hold another meeting at 6:00 pm this Friday (1st) and will convene a meeting of team captains at 6:00 pm next Friday (8th). Both meetings will still be held at the Western Youth Association.

International Relief Association Discusses Holding Charity Football

The International Relief Association of this city plans to continue the method of last year and hold a grand charity football match. A meeting of directors was held at 5:30 pm yesterday at the association's headquarters in Baxianqiao, attended by Li Guiyong, Gao Huaide, Chen Zhongen, Li Baojun, and others. As a result of the discussion, the competition method, date, and location will be decided after a staff member contacts the Western League. In addition, the Refugee Production and Consumption Cooperative originally planned to invite the Lido and Donghua, two strong Chinese teams, for a friendly match, with all ticket revenue used for the cooperative's expenses. After contacting the Western League, it was temporarily difficult to realize due to the lack of venues. If the venue problem is resolved, the Western League will also support it.

Amateur Sports Association Formally Established Yesterday; Cha Ruilong and Others Elected as Standing Directors

Martial artist Cha Ruilong has recently researched a type of martial art called New Combat, which is not limited by boxing manuals and can maximize physical strength and improve health. It is indeed a new discovery in the national martial arts community. In order to make this New Combat widely available to the public, the Amateur Sports Research Association has been organized to solicit members and publicly teach this New Combat within the association. The association was formally established yesterday, and Cha Ruilong, Xi Zhikai, Feng Zhiyin, Shi Zhengzhong, Liu Yongfu, Yu Liren, Wang Tiyu, Li Yizhu, Yu Yimin, and Lu Ruiqing were elected as standing directors. Gong Zhikai will serve as the secretary-general. The temporary office is located at No. 20 Jiqingli, North Shaanxi Road. Once the official address is determined, Mr. Cha will guide the members in practicing New Combat.

Finance: Exchange Rate Market Initially Tight, Then Slightly Recovers

The foreign exchange market situation yesterday: The HSBC exchange rate was announced, with British gold shrinking by .25, calculated at 4.5 shillings, and the US exchange rate at .375, which was 7.3125 yuan. Other rates also declined uniformly. The gray market for British and American exchange rates was initially tight, resembling the end of last week. However, the market atmosphere was volatile and uncertain, and people were uneasy. Banks did not discuss transactions much. In the after-market, the bid and ask prices differed by as much as half a yuan. The market suddenly loosened significantly in the afternoon, due to rumors that someone would be reappointed as the Chinese Minister of Finance. After Hong Kong telegrams denied it, it softened again, so the situation was extremely chaotic. In the morning, the British rate opened and immediately decreased by .03125, and the American rate also softened by .0625. Later, because Chinese commercial banks and others began to aggressively buy, and importers had an urgent need to settle foreign cotton, the foreign banks' willingness to supply was weak, causing the situation to tighten without any recovery. In an instant, the British rate retreated to 4.75 shillings, and the American rate also tightened to 7.6875 yuan. Although it stabilized slightly later, it was still difficult to sustain due to the continued arrival of buyers, eventually reaching a tight price of 4.6875 shillings and 7.625 yuan. Fortunately, Hong Kong telegrams came to offer sales, and a portion of the Chinese commercial long positions had already reached the point of profit-taking and were eager to settle at a high price, which suddenly increased the available funds, and the market situation took a turn. Extending to the noon close, the British gold recovered to 4.78125 shillings, and the US exchange rate loosened to 7.8125 yuan. It is said that Hong Kong intermediaries were selling British and buying American, with the British-American exchange rate set at 3 yuan, 9 jiao, 1 fen, 5 li, and 6 hao. In the afternoon, due to the rumors mentioned above, buying disappeared instantly, and sellers took over. The market opened and immediately loosened, reaching 4.90625 shillings and 8.125 yuan for the American exchange rate. However, after Hong Kong telegrams stated that this news was inaccurate, people's minds changed again, and it softened back to 4.8125 shillings, and closed at 7.875 yuan. As a result, the British rate was softer than the American rate, with the British rate softer by .09375 and the American rate by .125. After the close, it was heard that it had tightened again to 4.78125 shillings and 7.8125 yuan. The trend for futures was no different from the spot market.

HSBC Exchange Rate Shrinks

In the early morning, there were no telegrams for the London large bars or the Bank of America price. The London raw gold remained unchanged, and the exchange rate between British and American rates was even, and between British and French rates was also even. The rate shrank by .125 against Shanghai, the American rate fell by half a point against British, fell .2 jiao against Shanghai, and fell by .375 against French. The central exchange rate remained the same. The bank opened the spot selling price in the morning, with British gold at 4.875 shillings and the US exchange rate at 7.9375 yuan, which was .03125 tighter for British and .0625 softer for American than last Saturday. After the opening, foreign banks' willingness to sell remained weak, while Chinese banks and speculators came to settle deals, and there was still a need to settle foreign cotton, causing the market to suddenly tighten significantly. By 9:30, the British gold had softened to 4.75 shillings, and the US exchange rate had also tightened to 7.6875 yuan. The HSBC exchange rate was announced, with British gold shrinking by .25 and the US exchange rate by .375. The silver balance tax was announced, with no increase or decrease. After that, it stabilized for a while, but soon the buying wave rose again. The softest British gold had been called at 4.6875 shillings, and the tightest American exchange rate had also been called at 7.625 yuan. Later, Hong Kong telegrams came to supply sales, and many Chinese merchants also took advantage of the high prices to exit, so the underlying trend stopped tightening and remained stable. Extending to the noon close, the British gold had recovered to 4.78125 shillings, and the US exchange rate had also loosened to 7.8125 yuan, with the British continuing to tighten by .09375 and the American rate softening by .125 compared to the morning open.

Selling Wave Rises Again in the After-Market

The after-market was initially stable, but soon rumors spread in the market that Mr. Song would be reappointed as Minister of Finance, and sellers rose in unison. Moreover, foreign banks' appetite was very weak, and the market was extremely chaotic. The most stable Chinese Chamber of Commerce sold a small amount of spot American exchange rate to a foreign bank for 8.125 yuan. The British gold had also softened to 4.90625 shillings. At that time, many December 8 yuan Chinese settlements were completed, all of which were absorbed by foreign banks. After the entry, the above news was suddenly denied by a telegram from Hong Kong, so the selling wave gradually subsided, and foreign firms such as Xinfeng and Hesheng took the opportunity to buy in, and the situation tightened again. As a result, the British was uniformly tightened by .09375 and the American rate was uniformly softened by .125 compared to the end of last week. It was heard that after the close, the British gold continued to tighten to 4.78125 shillings and the US exchange rate shrank to 7.8125 yuan again.

Closely Following the Foreign Exchange to Transfer, Gold Shakes Unsteadily; There is a Fluctuation of 145 Yuan Throughout the Day

Yesterday's spot and gray market situation for cash gold: People were bewildered, and buying and selling followed the trend, causing prices to rise and fall rapidly. From morning to night, there was a difference of 145 yuan. Initially, with the exchange market continuing to tighten and soften, the buying interest was still strong. Under competitive purchases, it initially jumped 40 yuan to 3,900 yuan, and then rose another 45 yuan. Later, when the foreign exchange stabilized somewhat, a certain gold firm and the head of the silver shops agreed to sell, and general retail investors also thought of profit-taking and exiting, so the situation changed, and the price immediately retreated to within the 3,900 yuan mark to 3,885 yuan. Then, with the exchange market showing a soft state again, securities firms and currency exchange firms entered the market to aggressively buy, and many retail investors who had sold also entered again, and the buying wave reignited. It was also heard that Hong Kong intermediaries were active, and the price soared to 3,950 yuan, the highest price of the day. By noon, the foreign exchange reported even, and buying was inferior to selling, so the noon close was only 3,925 yuan. In the afternoon, the market situation suddenly changed, and the opening fell to 3,870 yuan, because the market rumored that Song Ziwen would be reappointed as Minister of Finance, and everyone had the intention to sell, and the foreign exchange also tended to harden. Securities firms and retail investors spat out a lot. The lowest plunged to 3,805 yuan. However, the foreign exchange still tightened and softened, and the Hong Kong telegram had denied the previous rumor, and a certain currency exchange firm and the silver shops were pulling the price, rising to 3,880 yuan at the close. After the close, the foreign exchange continued to soften, and a certain silver shop pulled the price up again, reaching 3,895 yuan. Transactions were brisk, about 2,700 taels. The silver shop's jewelry gold result hung high by 5 yuan, and the customs gold remained even.

Free Talk

Literature and Art and Life

— Wen Ge

A blind man touching an elephant's tail said that the elephant was smaller than a mouse. This uses a part to determine the whole, which is naturally wrong. The view of life is the same; although it is an abstract thing, there is also a distinction between part and whole. A true view of life: cannot use part to determine the whole but should use the whole to determine the part. But although the part is unified in the whole, it is also contradictory. If we ignore its contradiction and exaggerate its unity, then the story of the blind man determining the elephant with the tail is an example.

Many people say that literary works aim to reflect real life, which is an iron fact. We can refine life and expand our world view. But here, we must pay attention to the relationship between part and whole. If we do not pay attention, we will inevitably distort the view of life, making the part overly expanded, but making the whole blurred.

For example, in the case of Andreyev, he saw a lot of the ugliness of life. So in his works, there is only a mournful moan of despair for life. In fact, although life has a broad dark side, it is not entirely so. There is also a bright side that stands in opposition.

As for Chekhov, another pessimistic writer, he is slightly different from Andreyev. He is a man who deeply understands human nature and weaknesses, so he also expresses an irreparable sadness for life. However, he is not as completely despairing as Andreyev. In the gloom, he still hopes that the distant future will be better. However, the air of doubt in this hope is too strong, so the real light is still quite far from him.

Generally speaking, what these two writers see of life and the world cannot be considered wrong. Unfortunately, they are too attached to the part, so that for the whole, they cannot see clearly, like looking at flowers in the fog. The conclusion, of course, becomes a problem.

In fact, there is nothing in the universe that is forever unchanging, and the same is true of darkness and light. If we do not express despair for life, then even if everything around is dark, we do not need to be afraid or anything. As long as you can work hard and fight against it tirelessly, the light will always come one day. It is true that sometimes we may inevitably be sacrificed in fierce battles, but it is also good to be able to provide convenience for those who come later. So for Chekhov and Andreyev, I always feel infinitely regretful.

Here, it makes me think of Gorky, who is very different from them. He understands that the world has a dark side. But he does not express pessimism. On the contrary, he uses a more tenacious force to find the root of the darkness and break it. He once said, "We cannot but live in this life. We must recognize it. We must transform it." How correct these words are! They pierce the hearts of pessimists sharply!

Literary works have a great influence on people's thoughts. Of course, the world view presented must also be very accurate. Otherwise, there will inevitably be many people with weak wills who will be confused, resulting in a painful tragedy. What is the point of this? So, for every writer, I think they should objectively and wholly point out the world view.

Sally

— Xu Ye

The flowing water of the Volga River flows day and night, the source of this water is in the Valdai Hills. On the riverbank, there are boatmen with heroic songs morning and evening. This free port, which was once completed with the blood of millions of iron palms, is given the name: Great Russia's River of Blood.

In winter, the sound of the river is even more furiously agitated. Dazzling snowflakes spread evenly on the sandy plain, and not far away you can hear the sounds of the shepherdess and the sheep breathing, what a delightful atmosphere unfolding around the river.

Waterbirds skimming the surface of the waves, they flock to the windmills in the village, and after the snow, the moorland pansies exude an intoxicating fragrance, and the October sun kisses the vast mountains and river embankments. Beneath the green clouds, the river stretches out red waves, and the heroic roar of the waves is worth the love and praise of men and women growing up in a free country...

Here, I met Sally. She takes care of ten sheep, but she loves the roaring waves of the Volga, and she always brings the sheep here every day.

"Good morning!"

Sally is a courageous child.

"Tell me the story of the Volga again!"

The setting sun links a line of bright rays of light, the sound of animals' footsteps blows up from the pine forest, the shadows of travelers are reflected on the rapids of the river, the pasture at dusk slowly becomes quiet, the cold current loses its old attitude, and the arrival of the night feels extraordinarily gloomy.

"Would you like to breathe the wind of the quiet night?"

I look at her intently, and Sally smiles as she looks at the feathered shadows in the clouds.

Leaving the riverbank, her pace is very slow, the sheep accompany this traveler in the sandy plain, and Sally's amber-like eyes still stare at a vast starry sky.

"It's a thing of the past: the blood of our ancestors was spilled all over this river, there were such amazing days: the sufferers under the iron prison began a heroic action, for which we wanted freedom and sunshine!"

Sally spoke and sang: "I love the sun of the motherland, its dazzling brilliance! We forever sing on the bright earth, building the bright castle with solid strength..."

I am unusually moved.

"I hope I can have a day to shed blood!"

She laughed and clapped her hands at me.

In the night sky, under the moonlight, Sally shouted at the sheep and left. The coolness of the moorland was very strong. I looked at the few lights in the village from afar...

"We'll see you tomorrow!" The loud voice echoed in the high air.

The tide of blood涌着chest, in the confusing摸案中I woke up: 　视着future, silent 　念now adding greater courage, although there is no reed flute to harmonize with Sally's heroic song. For her, I will use battle to answer the call of the motherland!

……

At dawn, Sally came again.

"Remember: bright red exotic flowers will bloom in the sandy plain. Soon I will give you a pair of straw shoes. There are blood stains that I have shed!"

Looking up, eagles are chasing the　　white clouds, and the Volga River is surging again...

Oh! I have a source of endless life!

"Believing in Beauty Is Not My Land"

— Ze Fu

These past few days, every morning, I can often see florists on the street, carrying chrysanthemums of various colors and patterns. So fashionable halls and rooms often have chrysanthemum embellishments.

But I often have two kinds of musings about these chrysanthemums: chrysanthemums standing in magnificent halls will not be more beautiful.

Sure enough, my musings were not wrong. One day, I went to a certain restaurant to eat the wedding banquet of relatives, the ceremony hall was decorated very beautifully, and the guests were full of joy. Everyone was in high spirits, simply wanting to make a commotion until late at night. There were also a few pots of chrysanthemums in this ceremony hall, but they were all drooping like they were depressed, not as bright as the ones I saw in the morning at the florist's stall. The leaves were dry and the flowers were curled up. People will go to the middle of the night, I see the spirit is still each glowing, guessing punches and drinking wine, squeezing to see the bride, talking about business and making money, there is still not one that has some haggard appearance. Then why would the chrysanthemums be like this? It was originally standing in a pot, and there was soil in the pot. Although there was less, it would not be insufficient to supply its daily needs! That's right, I think chrysanthemums standing in magnificent ceremony halls will not be more beautiful.

With this experience, every time I pass in front of a restaurant, I pay more attention to the cypress and the like placed in front of their doors, which are indeed always so green and lovely. There are often a few pots of mixed flowers on the terrace of the house across from me, and I have never seen them withered or haggard, although sometimes they encounter strong winds and heavy rains, the flowers and leaves may fall a little, but the flower branches are still standing upright, with no sign of decline.

Chrysanthemums are originally famous for being proud of the frost, as Su Dongpo said, "The lotus has exhausted and there is no umbrella to hold the rain, and the chrysanthemum remains with branches proud of the frost." Even if it is being pressed by the cold frost, it is still blooming brightly. It basically does not want comfort, it wants to struggle with the environment, so it does not want to take advantage of spring and summer to compete with the various flowers for beauty. It must wait until after the sisters have already silenced and disappeared before it slowly spits out its unique beauty. Its aloofness is certainly admirable, and its fearlessness of oppression and independent struggle can make people infinitely admire it. Because its nature is like this, so what comfortable and magnificent halls and rooms, it is in fact repulsive to it.

If chrysanthemums were really like people, I think it would definitely announce people's sins, and it would shout even more, "Believing in beauty is not my land," and leave the halls and still go to struggle arduously with the storm.

Compilation of "Frontier Songs" (Book Review)

— Ruo Hong

Music possesses a great and moving power. A song of gentle affection, pleasing to the ear, can evoke boundless reverie; a heroic and stirring melody can cause the blood to boil. Since the War of Resistance, it has become even more evident that music and song not only manipulate individual emotions, but also grasp the soul of the entire nation. Its power cannot be extinguished, and countless singing groups have sprung up like mushrooms after the rain. This lies precisely in this fact. In the rear areas, singing is used to connect with the simple people and to educate the ignorant. It has reaped the effects of propaganda and improved the level of knowledge. On the front lines, many comrades have been inspired by singing and strengthened their courage. At this time, our country's music has entered a new stage. It has contributed its greatest strength to the War of Resistance, it has encouraged much public morale, and it has also recorded many touching and praiseworthy historical events.

Shanghai had a period of extreme fervor. Almost every program on the radio stations broadcasted songs of national salvation, and every corner resonated with exciting songs. However, as the armies retreated westward, everything fell into silence due to the special circumstances. All that could be heard were the "songs of national subjugation" that had been banned in earlier years. Since then, few pieces with any meaning have been seen.

By chance, in a small bookstore, I obtained a small booklet, which was "Frontier Songs," a recent work by the young composer Lao Xin. It is thin, only twenty-four pages, containing twenty-three new songs, divided into four parts. The lyrics are subtly powerful, but the simplicity does not diminish the connotation of the words and music. The songs are all easy to sing, especially the songs in "Compilation of Little Mosquitoes," which are especially suitable for singing materials for junior high and elementary school students. The musical scores are all in optimistic, cheerful, resolute, and passionate tones, full of confidence in the victory of the War of Resistance. "We have a common ideal, we have a common belief, advancing toward a common goal, our will is as strong as steel." These are the lyrics of the Graduation Song of Thousands of Li. What will the masses who love singing think when they see them?

Facing Life

— Xiang

Don't be afraid of fate playing tricks on you, just wipe away the dejected tears; like a piece of iron, the occasional rust on the outside cannot conceal the hardness in its core.

No matter how tightly the pain of words presses, take a breath, clench your fist, grit your teeth, every hope must be arranged by yourself, breaking through the persecution that fills the world.

The past was a period of rotten time, why should the living cling to skeletons? A guaranteed future lies before you, step into the dilapidated present.

Perhaps there is also a lingering, undying love—who dares to guarantee it for you in these times? The world originally had a bright and beautiful flower bud, but unfortunately it was destroyed yesterday.

Life is the crucible of the times, the crucible does not allow you any hesitation; a burst of boiling—a flash of light, dull steel is refined from a pile of rusty iron.

Entertainment Circle

Kun Opera Advocates Good and Punishes Evil—Beneficial to Worldly Morality and People's Hearts

— Shi Yiren

The way of sound is the most deeply moving, its transitions and shifts are invariably related to the rise and fall of world affairs. During the Ming Dynasty, Liang Bolong, Wei Liangfu, Zhang Xiaoquan, Ji Jingpo, and their like, were able to harmonize sounds and transform tones like gossamer, creating Kunqu opera. At that time, "The Red Pear Record" and "The Swallow Letter" were popular in the old capital. By the early Qing Dynasty, men of letters and poets competed to write legends and also compose scripts. "A Handful of Snow," "A Thousand Zhong of Fortune," and "Iron Crown Map," and others, propagated loyalty and righteousness, and their noble spirit soared to the skies; while "Emerald Garden," "Fisherman's Joy," "A Penny," and "The Gorgeous Cloud Pavilion," and other plays, all contained the intention of promoting good deeds, which could make the people's customs honest and upright. By the mid-Qianlong period, there was no alley in the marketplace that did not have someone who could sing the melodies; but today, the morale of the scholars is declining, weeds are everywhere, loyalty, righteousness, and morality have vanished; the music of the law has been destroyed, the upright spirit has disappeared, and the new plays compiled by actors all focus on romantic affairs in boudoirs, or show off novelty and compete for skill, supplemented by scenery, without considering whether the times are in harmony with the scenery. The audience rarely has the ability to judge, and they are only amused and pleased by the songs and banners for a time. However, as society declines, and human relations and customs become increasingly depraved, how can one find the correct standards and norms?

"The Water Margin Record," "Capturing Alive with Tea Borrowed," writes about Zhang Sanlang seducing a woman to the point of mutual destruction; "Qin Pick and Joyful Poem" originally belongs to a scholar living alone without company, and when he meets a wonderful nun, it is like a magnet attracting a needle, but he does not forget his ambition for fame, and eventually achieves success and returns, and then they unite as husband and wife. It is similar to "Romance of the West Chamber" in different ways; "Luo Meng" advises people not to be greedy for money; "Forced Divorce in a Fool's Dream" warns women to be chaste and patient, and not to be fickle. "White Gauze Shirt" tells of the evil retribution of bandits, and that a good wife, a righteous husband, and a filial son will have a day of reunion. Others, such as the wise wife of "Pipa Ji" reuniting, and the filial piety of "Jingchai Ji" being rewarded generously, all have a great impact on the hearts of the audience, so I say that if people's hearts can tend toward Kun Opera, abandon frivolity, and embark on the right path, the world will be able to enjoy prosperity. In the past, compiling and creating plays took a lot of effort, and they were corrected several times before they could be published and circulate in the world, and they were made with purpose. Even the legend "The Palace of Eternal Life" written by Hong Sheng of Qiantang took more than ten years of effort and was revised three times before it was completed, so it should be able to be passed down to future generations. The licentious atmosphere in Shanghai was extremely prevalent for a time, and gentlemen of great refinement should make corrections, how can they abandon the fundamentals and pursue the trivial?

Hollywood Movie News

— Fang Mu

Loretta Young and David Niven are very good friends, and their friendship has been going on for more than five years. She helped him engage in camera work, and they can be said to have like-minded goals and matching drums. Now they are working together in a film called "Eternally Yours," which adopts a universally pleasing theme, full of light and joy. Their advantages are all brought into full play.

No one dares to say that Hollywood directors and screenwriters are not opportunists. An interesting joke was made during the filming of "The Housekeeper's Daughter." Originally: There was a scene shot on location on the streets of New York with a violent fight and arson, the scene was realistic and lively enough. But as a result, someone called to report to the police that there was trouble on the street, and it was turned upside down! The bureau received the report and sent a large number of police, navy, and fire trucks, marching mightily to the scene of the incident. As a result, the scene was made even more tense, but it was all filmed by the producers. Naturally, there was no need for another N, G, and the adventurous parties had a very good harvest as a result.

Since the outbreak of the European War this time, the people of Europe have been very depressed and need some comfort and stimulation! In the entertainment circles of Britain and France, naturally, performances of tragedies are not welcome, and light comedies are generally used instead, which will bring smiles to the audience and temporarily forget their worries.

Regarding movies, the American Artists Association sent four suitable films for the same good. The four types are: 1. "Intermezzo" starring Leslie Howard 2. "Eternally Yours" by Loretta Young 3. "The Housekeeper's Daughter" by Joan Bennett 4. "A Chump at Oxford" by Laurel and Hardy.

A Scene from Mr. Wang and Three Tenants

(Produced by Hua Xin Company, Screening at Xin Guang)

New Work Introduction

The Toy Wife

— Qi Hua

Louise Rainer's acting skills, starting from "The Great Ziegfeld," have received the highest praise for any work, her profound inner performance, Hollywood does not seem to have an actress who can rival her. Louise Rainer in "The Toy Wife" plays a wayward, active girl who even regards marriage as child's play. From when her father takes her sisters back to the New Orleans plantation, she meets George, her sister Louise's childhood lover; she socializes with Andre; the years after marriage; Louise's jealousy of managing the household; her elopement with Andre; and finally, lying sick in a hostel, begging Louise to marry George before her death and raise her beloved son, Louise Rainer fully sculpted a "Toy Wife" as envisioned by the playwright.

Director Subi also devoted his full efforts to assist Louise Rainer in sculpting, so in his delicate and moving paintings, we only feel that there are many scenes that are not fully developed, rather than the drawbacks of being tedious. For example, the love process between Gilbert and George; and the desolate scene after eloping with Andre, etc., are not fully depicted, so the following examples all show the director's meticulousness. (1) Louise comes down the stairs and sees George coming out of her father's room. She just wants to turn back, but George stops her, but George tells her that he loves Gilbert. After Louise blesses them, when they kiss, a cutaway shot shows Andre just seeing this sad scene at the door. (2) George and Andre duel, the director only writes about Gilbert getting out of the carriage and hearing two loud bangs, she covers her face and weeps. (3) Louise asks George to go to the hostel to see Gilbert, George waits below, but finally moves upstairs. Other depictions of sisterly affection are also very lovely.

Melvyn Douglas's George is very moving as he witnesses his wife's neglect of the household and asks Louise to come home to preside over the household, he cannot bear to blame his beloved wife and is grateful for Louise's kindness. Beulah Bondi's Louise sacrifices her own happiness and always thinks of her sister, and her performance is also very moving.

— Chun Guang

Guohua's costume film "Hero in Troubled Times", as the name suggests, is known to be a big film. It is now more than half completed. The male leads are Shu Shi, Bai Yun, Zheng Zhong, You Guangzhao, and Zhou Qi. The female leads are Zhou Manhua, Chen Jingfang, Xu Tianren, and Meng Na. The lineup is very strong and the capital is also huge.

Another costume work "Dong Xiaowan" is in preparation, and the protagonist is Zhou Xuan. She came to the company the other day to try on new costumes.

Wu Cun's new work is "The Amorous History of Su San", and he has been busy planning the scenery, costumes and selecting actors these days.

In addition to filming, the actors have also been rushing to rehearse the Peking opera "Killing Home While Fishing" and the drama, preparing to show their talents in the Shanghai Refugee Association charity show on the Xinxin stage.

— Paul

This film tells the story of a famous reporter in the American press, Stanley, who was employed by the New York Herald and was sent to Africa to find a missing expert missionary Livingston. As a result, he finally found Livingston due to his unremitting efforts. It caused a sensation in the United States and was enough to encourage people to have a spirit of courage, perseverance, and indomitable will. Spencer Tracy plays Stanley. The whole film is great and compact. The Daguanming will be released next time. The left image is one of the tense scenes in the film. It is the latest woodcut.

Unofficial History of the Pear Garden

— Xu Muyun

The North and South each have a worship

Who knew that Old Rui's eyes were dim and he didn't see it, he still straightened his waist and walked straight forward. At this time, the doctor froze there, unable to sit down or stand. At the same time, all the male and female guests in the ballroom focused their eyes on Mei's side, and the dancers sitting beside him felt even more embarrassed. I couldn't bear to look at it from the opposite side, so I quickly stood up, caught up with Old Rui, and announced "Boss Mei is saying hello to you." He hurriedly turned back, took off his hat and politely returned the salute to Lanfang, exchanged a few words of greetings, and then I accompanied him out together. Often there are many people who don't know Debao, wondering what kind of person he is with that bald head and chubby body. Why is Dr. Mei so respectful to him? In fact, when Old Rui sang eight volumes of "Hun Yuan Box" in the past, he played the protagonist Zhang Tianshi. The insignificant mussel spirit who played with him was the famous Dr. Mei today. Mei can respect the predecessors of the Pear Garden. It is the greatest reason for his success. Other children's ability, and status are far worse than Mei's in every way, but the arrogance of those people is a hundred times faster than Lanfang. Therefore, I say that today's drama is really reluctant to watch. Even the younger actors visiting guests, I am also reluctant to talk to them. (150)
